You can use known intent signals to tailor your marketing and sales efforts more effectively to meet the needs of high-intent leads and prospects. When de-anonymized, these intent signals can be the key to uncovering hidden opportunities, understanding market trends, and identifying potential leads. 6sense’s Intent Data platform can provide comprehensive insights into buyer behavior by identifying, aggregating, and analyzing intent signals. By analyzing intent signals, 6sense can help you identify and target those in-market opportunities more efficiently. Insights derived from intent signals enable businesses to enhance personalization efforts by understanding the unique preferences and behaviors of individual customers. Intent signals identified by 6sense can help you determine the most promising prospects, tailor your messaging to their needs and interests, and engage them with timely and relevant offers.\n\nTitle: Predictive Buying Stages - 6sense Support\nURL: https://support.6sense.com/docs/predictive-buying-stages\nContent: Predictive buying stages help you prioritize leads, accounts, and opportunities. ### Target buying stage (intent score 0–19). The Target stage is for accounts currently showing little to no activity. ### Awareness buying stage (intent score 20-49). The Awareness stage is for accounts that are showing some level of activity and should be treated as top of funnel/early stage. We suggest you target accounts in this stage for broad-based engagements. ### Consideration buying stage (intent score 50-69). The Consideration stage shows accounts exhibiting more significant activity compared to their baseline, with a longer history of above-average engagement. ### Decision buying stage (intent score 70-85). Accounts in the Decision stage show significant digital research activity levels across data sources. ### Purchase buying stage (intent score 86-100). The Purchase stage is for accounts at the bottom of the marketing funnel and those most likely to open an opportunity soon. Predictive analyzes different signals to determine where an account is categorized in a buying stage.\n\nTitle: A Beginner's Guide to Predictive Analytics for Marketing and Sales\nURL: https://6sense.com/platform/predictive-analytics/the-guide-to-predictive-analytics/\nContent: Predictive analytics is a forward-looking application of data that can decipher what your buyers are doing in real-time, and the likelihood of them becoming a customer. This is where the *Stalled Deal Index* comes in. The Stalled Deal Index treats it as risk. ## **What Is the Stalled Deal Index?**. At its core, the Stalled Deal Index (SDI) is a momentum KPI. Start by calculating your **Average Time-in-Stage** for closed-won deals. A deal is considered *stalled* when it exceeds the average Time-in-Stage by **20% or more**. The **Stalled Deal Index** is the percentage of total pipeline deals that exceed that threshold. If the next step is vague or rep-owned, the deal is stalled. When teams actively manage the Stalled Deal Index, the impact compounds fast. The Stalled Deal Index shifts your focus from static stages to dynamic movement—where revenue is actually created. How does MEDDICC compare against other qualification frameworks? The first thing to note is that MEDDICC is different from most qualification frameworks for one fundamental reason:MEDDICC sees the qualification as a process that occurs throughout your deal’s lifecycle. In contrast, most other frameworks see qualification as a one-time event or a stage that you have to pass.An excellent example of the divide between MEDDICC and other frameworks can be found by comparing MEDDICC to BANT, which is the most popular qualification framework used by sellers.MEDDICC versus BANT IBM developed BANT in the 1950’s, and despite being over 60 years old, BANT is still widely used by sellers and for a good reason. BANT quickly orientates the seller onto four elements that will quickly help to identify if the customer is qualified to buy.BANT is based on the acronym:B – Budget: Does the customer have the budget available to them?A – Authority: Does the customer have the authority to buy?N – Need: Does the customer have enough need (pain) to buy?T –  ... Whether  ...    MEDDIC was created at PTC (a software company) in the 1990s and helped them grow from $300M to $1B in four years. February 28, 2026\n\n---\n\n## Why Rigorous Deal Reviews Matter Most sales teams lose deals they should have disqualified weeks earlier. They invest time, resources, and emotional energy into opportunities that were never going to close, not because the product was wrong, but because the deal fundamentals were never validated. A structured deal review forces honesty. It surfaces the gaps between what you hope is true and what you have actually confirmed. It prevents happy ears from turning into missed quarters. And it gives sales leadership the information they need to coach effectively rather than just asking \"when is this going to close?\" This checklist combines MEDDPICC-style qualification with practical deal management criteria. Use it in weekly pipeline reviews, in one-on-ones with your manager, and as a personal gut-check before updating your forecast. ## Deal Qualification Scorecard\n\nScore each criterion from 0-3 using the definitions below: | Score | Definition |\n| --- | --- |\n| 0 | Not identified or not started |\n| 1 | Partially identified, unconfirmed | | 2 | Identified and confirmed by prospect |\n| 3 | Fully validated with evidence | ### MEDDPICC Criteria | Criterion | Questions to Validate | Score (0-3) |\n| --- | --- | --- | | Metrics | Have you quantified the business impact of the problem? Does the prospect agree with your numbers? | | Economic Buyer | Have you identified and engaged the person with budget authority? Have they confirmed interest? | | Decision Criteria | Do you know the formal and informal criteria the committee will use to decide? | | Decision Process | Can you describe every step from today to signed contract, including who approves at each stage? |  ...    | Total Score | Deal Health | Action |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| 20-24 | Strong | Accelerate and close | | 14-19 | Promising | Address gaps in your next interactions | | 8-13 | At risk | Develop a recovery plan or consider disqualifying |  ...    ### Stakeholder Mapping Status  ...    ## Step-by-Step Instructions\n\n### Running a Weekly Deal Review Prepare before the meeting. Fill out the scorecard for each deal in your pipeline before sitting down with your manager. Come with an honest assessment, not an optimistic one. Start with the score. Present the total MEDDPICC score for each deal. This immediately surfaces which deals need attention and which are progressing well. Focus on gaps, not updates. The deal review is not a status update. It is a strategy session. Spend your time on the criteria scored 0-1, not rehashing what is going well. Define specific next actions. For every gap identified, agree on a concrete next step with an owner and a deadline. \"I  ... Predictive deal scoringis an powerful data-driven method for estimating the likelihood of closing deals in your pipeline. Each deal is assigned a numerical score, with higher scores indicating a stronger chance of success. By analyzing patterns in your company’s historical sales data and ongoing activity, predictive deal scoring identifies what success looks like for your business and applies those insights to current deals. Unlike manual scoring—often based on intuition or incomplete information—predictive deal scoring analyzes deal data,  ...    Ensure sales, marketing, and customer success teams are on the same page with a unified, data-driven view of deal  ...    # How Dear Lucy’s Predictive Deal Scoring Works Dear Lucy's predictive deal scoring analyzes in real-time what winning looks like in your company over a rolling 12-month period. It compares open deals in your pipeline against this benchmark and assigns a score from 1 to 99 to each deal, indicating the likelihood of the deal closing successfully. To make insights even clearer, each deal is also given a star rating that highlights specific factors where the deal excels or where it may be at risk. This layered approach provides actionable guidance to help your team focus and take  ...    Our predictive deal scoring evaluates the following key factors:\n### **Total Activity Count** How active the deal has been in terms of calls, meetings, and tasks.\n### **Future Activity Count** Scheduled activities that indicate ongoing engagement.\n### **Recent Activity Count** The level of activity in the recent past.\n### **Deal Length**\nThe total time the deal has spent in the pipeline. ### **Deal Probability**\nLikelihood of closing, based on sales reps' input or CRM stage probabilities. ### **Time in Stage**\nHow long the deal has stayed in its current stage, signaling potential delays. ### **Close Date Change Count**\nThe frequency of changes to the expected close date.\n### **Deal Size** The total value of the deal.\n### **Overdue Day Count**\nDeals past their expected close date are flagged as risky. ### **Deal Value Change Count**\nAdjustments to the deal value. The algorithm continuously evaluates your pipeline and adapts as new data flows in, ensuring scores remain accurate and  ... Deal scores predict the probability of winning the open deals in your pipelines, which can help teams to prioritize and focus on deals with higher chances to close. Deal scores are powered by AI, which checks several factors to generate the score, including data from deal properties and activities. Please note: deal scores are for information only and shouldn't be used as the only factor in making business decisions. While HubSpot strives to ensure the accuracy and reliability of the scoring model, it may not always be  ...    The following deal properties are currently taken into consideration when generating a deal score: - Owner: the time spent without an owner and changes to the assigned owner. - Next step: the time since the deal's next step was updated. - Deal probability: the current deal probability and changes to the deal probability. - Activities: the time since an activity was logged or associated contacts were last contacted (via calls, emails, or  ...    - Deal stage: the time spent in the current stage.\n- Create date: the time since the deal was created.  ...    - Deals that are reopened will not receive a deal score. In these cases, it's recommended to create a new deal instead of re-opening a closed deal to get an accurate score. Please note: the deal stage is the source of truth to indicate a deal is closed. If you manually set a deal's probability to 0% or 100% rather than closing the deal, those deals will still receive deal scores. To stop a deal from  ...    With the introduction of buying signals, predictive deal scores factor in data related to activities.  ...    Subscription required A Sales Hub Professional or Enterprise subscription is required to view the deal score details using the hover function. You can access deal scores by adding the Deal score property as a column in a deals index page view, or by viewing the Deal score card on individual deal records. You can also segment deals based on their deal scores in index page views and deal-based segments. To view deal scores:\n\nIn the dialog box: - On the right, click and drag Deal Score to the desired position in your columns.  ...    1. To view more information about an individual deal's score, click the name of the deal, and navigate to the Deal score card. 2. To open the deal in preview, hover over a deal name and click Preview. Win Rates | Gong\nURL: https://www.gong.io/win-rates\nContent: # Understanding Win Rates – A Key to Sales Success. Win rate is a pivotal metric in sales, encapsulating the percentage of deals closed successfully compared to the total number dealt. Because understanding your win rate can transform how you approach sales forecasting, team performance, and resource allocation. ## What is a Win Rate? Sales organizations often break down win rates by different dimensions—be it by individual sales reps, teams, or different product lines—to pinpoint areas of strength and opportunity. ## Importance of Win Rates. Win rates serve as a fundamental indicator of a sales team’s health and prowess. High win rates may reflect a well-targeted sales strategy and a compelling product or service offering, whereas lower win rates could signal misalignments or market challenges. Improving win rates is about more than just enhancing numbers; it’s about building smarter, more strategic sales operations. ## See how Gong increases your win rates.\n\nTitle: Under the hood of deal likelihood scores - Gong Help Center\nURL: https://help.gong.io/docs/explainer-under-the-hood-of-deal-likelihood-scores\nContent: On average, Gong AI is 21% more precise than sales reps in predicting winning deals, as early as week 4 in the quarter. Let me compile the findings.\n\n---\n\n# Predictive Win/Loss Analysis into Real-Time Sales Enablement: Research Findings\n\n## 1. PREDICTIVE SALES ENABLEMENT PLATFORMS\n\n### Gong (Revenue AI Platform)\n- **Signals used**: Conversation transcripts (calls, emails, meetings), mentions of legal/pricing, competitor mentions, red flags in emails, deal warnings, call interaction stats, CRM data. Uses a machine learning model (not rule-based) trained on complete lifecycle of won and lost deals across its customer base.\n- **Recommendations to sellers**: AI-generated call summaries, at-risk opportunity flags, recommended actions to keep deals on track, real-time coaching during calls via scorecards, content cues. \"Deal likelihood scores\" update daily per deal.\n- **Accuracy**: Gong AI is **21% more precise than sales reps** in predicting winning deals, as early as week 4 in the quarter. AI-powered forecasting delivers **20% more accurate results** than CRM-only projections.\n- **CRM integration**: Native Salesforce, HubSpot integrations. All recordings indexed and searchable by rep, account, deal stage, keyword.\n- **Pricing**: $1,200-$2,400/seat/year (Vendr data). Gong Engage and Forecast modules add 20-40% on top of base. Multi-year discounts of 15-30% available.\n- **Healthcare IT applicability**: Applicable for any enterprise sales team including health IT. Conversation intelligence works across verticals.\n- **Key stat**: Deals without decision-makers are **80% less likely to close** (SMB) and **233% less likely** (enterprise).\n- **Sources**: https://help.gong.io/docs/explainer-under-the-hood-of-deal-likelihood-scores, https://www.gong.io/revenue-intelligence-software, https://www.vendr.com/marketplace/gong, https://www.gong.io/blog/heres-how-selling-to-decision-makers-affects-your-win-rates-ignore-at-your-own-risk\n\n### Clari (Revenue Orchestration Platform)\n- **Signals used**: 2 years of CRM opportunity history, conversation data, meeting data, rep/prospect email activity, meetings taking place, files/contracts exchanged. Applies AI against the full buying process, not just CRM data.\n- **Recommendations to sellers**: Opportunity Scoring provides a \"data-driven second opinion\" on deal health. Smart nudges via Clari Connect messaging or email alerts flag at-risk deals. \"Next best move\" guidance for each seller. Pipeline risk detection based on deal push count, opportunity age, deal size.\n- **Accuracy**: Claims to help reps focus on \"the right deals\" with AI-driven opportunity scores. Specific accuracy metrics not publicly published.\n- **CRM integration**: Deep Salesforce and Dynamics integration. Multiple CRM instances supported in single view.\n- **Pricing**: Enterprise pricing, not publicly listed. Typically $50-100+/user/month for enterprise tiers.\n- **Healthcare IT applicability**: Strong in enterprise sales environments. Used by large B2B organizations.\n- **Key insight**: Tracks total number of times a deal gets pushed out and incorporates that into AI-driven opportunity score.\n- **Sources**: https://www.clari.com/blog/crm-scoring/, https://www.clari.com/solutions/ai-sales-engagement-productivity/, https://pages.clari.com/rs/866-BBG-005/images/Clari-SB-AI-Applications-for-Sales-0917.pdf\n\n### 6sense (Intent Data + Predictive Buying Stages)\n- **Signals used**: Third-party intent data (web research behavior), first-party engagement, CRM data, G2 Buyer Intent, Bombora intent, behavioral signals across the internet. Analyzes signals at the **account level**, not contact level (this is a noted limitation).\n- **Recommendations to sellers**: Predictive Buying Stages with specific guidance per stage:\n  - **Target (0-19)**: Little/no activity -- broad awareness campaigns\n  - **Awareness (20-49)**: Top-of-funnel engagement\n  - **Consideration (50-69)**: More significant activity, deeper engagement\n  - **Decision (70-85)**: Significant digital research -- direct sales engagement\n  - **Purchase (86-100)**: Bottom of funnel -- close now\n- **Accuracy**: Intent scores 0-100 with defined buying stage thresholds. Predictive analytics combine engagement scores of key buyer personas.\n- **CRM integration**: Salesforce, HubSpot, Marketo integrations. G2 integration auto-maps buyer intent data.\n- **Pricing**: Enterprise pricing. Typically $60,000-$150,000+/year for mid-market.\n- **Healthcare IT applicability**: Strong for identifying hospitals/health systems actively researching EHR or health IT solutions. Intent data reveals when a prospect is \"in-market\" before they reach out.\n- **Sources**: https://6sense.com/platform/intent-data/what-are-intent-signals/, https://support.6sense.com/docs/predictive-buying-stages, https://6sense.com/platform/predictive-analytics/the-guide-to-predictive-analytics/\n\n### Aviso AI (Guided Selling Platform)\n- **Signals used**: CRM activity, email, calendars, daily chats, support and success tools. LiveStream real-time data sync across CRM and sales tools.\n- **Recommendations to sellers**: **30+ AI nudges** that guide proactive next steps on deals. MIKI (AI assistant) answers deal questions instantly. Next-best-action guidance per opportunity. Weekly persona digests and event-based updates via mobile, email, and platform notifications.\n- **Accuracy**: Claims **98%+ forecast accuracy**. States teams close **20% more deals** using guided selling vs. conventional CRM.\n- **CRM integration**: Integrates with Salesforce, Dynamics. Supports multiple CRM instances. Writeback auto-updates deal details, auto-logs rep activities, enriches CRM contacts.\n- **Pricing**: Enterprise pricing, not publicly listed.\n- **Healthcare IT applicability**: Applicable to complex B2B sales. Generative AI creates personalized outreach and objection handling for specific verticals.\n- **Sources**: https://www.aviso.com/product/deal-acceleration, https://www.aviso.com/platform, https://salestechstar.com/proactive-sales-engagement/aviso-launches-version-2-0-of-ai-guided-sales-platform-to-reimagine-the-sales-experience/\n\n### People.ai (Activity Intelligence)\n- **Signals used**: Automatically captures every email, meeting, and call -- writes back to CRM. AI-guided coaching **increased win rates by 36%** (GTM Performance Gap Report).\n- **CRM integration**: Salesforce, HubSpot, Microsoft integrations.\n- **Pricing**: Enterprise pricing, typically $35-75/user/month.\n- **Healthcare IT applicability**: Content recommendations and battlecards directly applicable to competitive health IT selling.\n- **Sources**: https://www.highspot.com/blog/ai-sales-coaching/, https://www.highspot.com/solutions/sales-enablement/, https://www.highspot.com/blog/ai-guided-selling/\n\n### Outreach (AI Revenue Platform + Deal Agent)\n- **Signals used**: 33 billion interaction signals/week across 6,000+ customers. Source: https://gptfy.ai/resources/salesforce-ai-use-cases/deal-coach/\n\n---\n\n## 2. REAL-TIME DEAL COACHING\n\n### Key Concepts from Research\n\n**Next Best Action (NBA)** is the dominant paradigm. Defined as: \"A prioritized action recommendation based on signals, risk, and stage context.\" NBA differs from lead scoring -- it prescribes a **specific action**, not just a priority score.\n\n**How NBA Works** (3-stage pipeline per HALIRO):\n1. **Data aggregation**: CRM, marketing automation, sales engagement, third-party intent signals\n2. **Behavior modeling**: ML algorithms analyze historical journeys to identify action sequences that led to conversions\n3. **Recommendation generation**: Real-time evaluation of each account, generating prioritized recommendations contextualized to deal stage, decision-maker profile, and recent activity\n\n**Key finding**: NBA adoption often fails for non-technological reasons. The #1 pitfall is \"confusing automation with prescription\" -- NBA proposes, the sales rep decides. Systems that try to impose actions get ignored.\n\n**Win rate improvements from AI coaching** (aggregated across sources):\n- 20-25% improvement in rep proficiency (Whatfix)\n- 32% improvement in win rates from AI coaching programs (Whatfix)\n- 36% improvement in win rates (Highspot GTM Performance Gap Report)\n- 26-35% win rate increase when AI guides deals effectively (ValueSelling)\n- 7-15x ROI in first year of AI sales tools (ValueSelling)\n- 81% of AI-using sales teams report increased revenue (ValueSelling)\n\n**Sources**: https://haliro.io/en/blog/next-best-action-ia-guide-commerciaux-quotidien, https://whatfix.com/blog/ai-sales-coaching/, https://www.valueselling.com/selling-guides/ai-in-sales-guide, https://everworker.ai/blog/ai_next_best_action_sales_execution\n\n---\n\n## 3. PRESCRIPTIVE ANALYTICS IN SALES\n\n### Bain & Company Framework\nBain's research on prescriptive analytics in sales and marketing identifies the key architecture:\n- **CRM stage triggers prescribed activities**: When a rep notes a stage change, the system triggers a new set of prescribed activities for other decision-makers at the target company.\n- **Price optimization**: Analytics provides guidance on price levels and discounts based on market, competitive, internal, and customer-level data.\n- **Implementation approach**: \"Pick one micro-battle\" -- start with a narrowly defined topic like ideal customer profile, quantified market opportunity, or basic price target zones. Prove value, then expand.\n- **Source**: https://www.bain.com/insights/do-this-not-that-prescriptive-analytics-in-sales-and-marketing/\n\n### Predictive vs. Prescriptive (Tableau/Industry Consensus)\n- **Predictive**: \"What might happen?\" -- forecasts future outcomes from historical data\n- **Prescriptive**: \"What should we do?\" -- recommends specific actions based on predicted outcomes using AI/ML\n- Prescriptive analytics is the evolution FROM prediction TO action. The gap between knowing a deal is at 40% win probability and knowing what to DO about it is where prescriptive analytics lives.\n- **Source**: https://www.tableau.com/analytics/predictive-analytics-vs-prescriptive-analytics\n\n### Salesforce Einstein Guided Selling\nSalesforce's approach: Reps can ask Einstein \"Tell me what to do to close this deal\" and get a personalized close plan that accounts for buyer context, competitive dynamics, and deal history. Example: Einstein recommends sending a discounted bundle offer with a competitive comparison datasheet to outmaneuver a specific competitor.\n- **Source**: https://resources.salestechstar.com/STS-Salesforce-the-sales-ai-playbook-7-ways-ai-can-help-you-close-more-deals-EN.pdf\n\n---\n\n## 4. DEAL RISK SIGNALS AND EARLY WARNING\n\n### Top Risk Signals (Aggregated from Outreach, Pintel.AI, DemandZEN, Hive Perform, Zime AI, Amolino)\n\n**Leading Indicators (predict risk BEFORE it happens)**:\n1. **Stakeholder engagement dropping**: Meetings initiated by prospect vs. accepted; stakeholders added/removed from conversations\n2. **Time in stage exceeding benchmark**: Deal is \"stalled\" when it exceeds average time-in-stage by 20%+ (Stalled Deal Index methodology)\n3. **Close date pushed multiple times**: Each push increases loss probability\n4. **Lack of future activities scheduled**: No upcoming meetings/calls = dead deal\n5. **Decision-maker absence**: 80% lower close rate in SMB, 233% lower in enterprise (Gong data)\n6. **Vague or rep-owned next steps**: If next step is vague, the deal is stalled\n7. **Deal value shrinking**: Compression rate indicates weakening position\n8. **No activity in 14+ days**: \"Staleness\" metric\n9. **Competitor mentions increasing**: Conversation intelligence detects competitive risk\n10. **Pricing objections or timeline hesitation**: Real-time conversation signals\n\n**The Stalled Deal Index (SDI)**:\n- Calculate Average Time-in-Stage for closed-won deals\n- A deal is \"stalled\" when it exceeds that by 20%+\n- SDI = percentage of total pipeline deals exceeding threshold\n- Teams that actively manage SDI see compounding revenue impact\n- **Source**: https://demandzen.com/stalled-deal-index-b2b-sales-kpis/\n\n**72-Hour Rule**: When a stalled-qualified deal surfaces, the manager must identify the specific objection or engagement gap and work with the rep on a targeted next action within 72 hours.\n- **Source**: https://zime.ai/blogs/how-to-indentify-stalled-deals-early\n\n**Essential Pipeline Health Inputs for Any Forecasting Model**: Stage, time-in-stage, days since last activity, stakeholder engagement level (number of contacts, seniority, activity types), changes in deal size, changes in close date, historical conversion rates segmented by deal characteristics (source, segment, competitor).\n- **Source**: https://amolino.ai/resources/b2b-sales-forecast-accuracy-guide\n\n---\n\n## 5. DEAL QUALIFICATION FRAMEWORKS & PREDICTIVE ACCURACY\n\n### MEDDPICC (The Enterprise Standard)\n\n**Components**: Metrics, Economic Buyer, Decision Criteria, Decision Process, Paper Process, Implicate the Pain, Champion, Competition\n\n**Predictive accuracy data**:\n- Forecast accuracy improves from **60-70% to 85-95%** with MEDDIC/MEDDPICC (multiple sources)\n- Average **win rate increases of 20-30%** with MEDDPICC (Salesmotion)\n- Patra case study: **143% increase in win rate**, 32% decrease in time-to-close, 48% increase in average deal size\n- Frontify: **35% increase in win rates**\n- **18% higher win rates and 24% larger deal sizes** from full MEDDPICC adoption (Salesmotion)\n- Average **40% decrease in sales cycle length** and **35% increase in deal size** (MEDDIC Academy)\n- Early decision-maker involvement boosts win rates by **55%**; delayed engagement reduces win rates by **113%** (Ebsta/Pavilion 2025 Benchmarks)\n- Minimum score threshold of **70%+** before deal enters commit forecast is the single practice that improves forecast accuracy most\n\n**Best fit**: Deals >$100K ACV, 5+ stakeholders, 6+ month cycles, formal procurement, competitive markets\n\n### BANT (Lightweight Qualifier)\n- Budget, Authority, Need, Timeline\n- Best for: SMB/<$20K ACV, short cycles, high-volume qualification\n- Forecast accuracy improvement: Low\n- Training time: 1-2 hours\n\n### SPICED (Customer-Centric Alternative)\n- Situation, Pain, Impact, Critical Event, Decision\n- Better discovery questions than MEDDPICC\n- Pairs well as a hybrid: SPICED for discovery, MEDDPICC for pipeline management\n\n### Command of the Message (Force Management)\n- Outcome-focused framework for aligning solution to customer problems\n- Focuses on differentiation and value articulation\n- Complements MEDDPICC for deal qualification\n- AI tools now embed the methodology by analyzing calls for value-based language, auto-populating MEDDICC fields, and generating discovery questions per buyer persona\n\n**Hybrid Best Practice**: Use BANT for initial qualification by SDRs, SPICED for discovery conversations, MEDDPICC for pipeline management and forecasting. This is the emerging 2026 consensus.\n\n**Sources**: https://cro.expert/blog/sales-qualification-framework-enterprise, https://salesmotion.io/blog/meddpicc-sales-methodology, https://salesmotion.io/blog/meddic-vs-meddpicc, https://meddicc.com/resources/meddicc-versus-other-qualification-frameworks-like-bant\n\n---\n\n## 6. THE \"DEAL SCORING CARD\" CONCEPT\n\n### Hoffman Scorecard (Proprietary)\n- A \"gives and gets\" framework where reps track what they've given (marketing materials, demos, pricing, trials, exec access, proposals, discounts) vs. what they've gotten (internal referral, cell phone, budget info, competition intel, technical win, champion, procurement intro, signed contract).\n- Score reveals deal health based on balance of gives/gets\n- Available through Closer Membership program\n- **Source**: https://sellhoffman.com/scorecard/\n\n### Demoshake Deal Review Checklist (MEDDPICC-Based Scorecard)\nScore each criterion 0-3:\n- **0**: Not identified or not started\n- **1**: Partially identified, unconfirmed\n- **2**: Identified and confirmed by prospect\n- **3**: Fully validated with evidence\n\nScoring tiers:\n- **20-24**: Strong -- accelerate and close\n- **14-19**: Promising -- address gaps in next interactions\n- **8-13**: At risk -- develop recovery plan or disqualify\n- **0-7**: Dead -- disqualify\n\nKey practice: \"Set score thresholds for forecast categories. 'Commit requires 18+'\" and track scoring accuracy over time by comparing scores to actual outcomes.\n- **Source**: https://demoshake.com/guides/deal-review-checklist\n\n### Fullcast Deal Health Score (Four-Pillar Model)\nBuilt on 4 pillars:\n1. **Qualification Strength** (MEDDPICC completion)\n2. **ICP Fit & Firmographics**\n3. **Deal Progression & Velocity** (time in stage, stage-to-stage conversion)\n4. **Engagement & Activity**\n\nScoring tiers:\n- **Red (0-49)**: Unhealthy, likely lost without intervention\n- **Yellow (50-79)**: At risk, needs attention\n- **Green (80-100)**: Healthy, high probability\n\nKey stat: 76% of companies using the right sales technology hit quota.\n- **Source**: https://www.fullcast.com/content/how-to-score-deal-health/\n\n### HubSpot Deal Score (AI-Powered, Built-In)\nFactors analyzed:\n- Owner assignment + duration\n- Next step recency\n- Deal probability and changes\n- Activity volume (calls, emails, meetings)\n- Deal stage and time in stage\n- Create date\n- Close date change count\n- Deal size\n\nScore: 0-100 with key factor breakdown (+/- indicators). Available in Sales Hub Professional/Enterprise. Score history tracked over time.\n- **Source**: https://knowledge.hubspot.com/records/use-deal-scores\n\n### Ricavvo AI Deal Scoring (Multi-Dimensional)\nEvaluates:\n- Risk Radar (competitors, external obstacles)\n- Readiness (technical prerequisites, timeline, resources)\n- Financial Fidelity (budget, approval process)\n- Business Impact Blueprint (defined need, potential ROI)\n- Decision-Making Maze (stakeholders, engagement, authority)\n\nProvides actionable insights: spots gaps, recommends next moves, adjusts probability in real-time.\n- **Source**: https://ricavvo.com/blog/cracking-the-code-ai-deal-scoring-sales-probability-predictions\n\n---\n\n## 7. HEALTHCARE IT SALES ENABLEMENT\n\n### Key Findings\n- **Oracle Health ranked #1** in Black Book 2024 State of Global Health IT & EHR Adoption across Patient Health Data Management, Communications, Order Entry, and Decision Support (score: 9.36/10 mean).\n- EHR vendor selection involves formal RFP processes, typically evaluated by cross-functional committees (IT, clinical, legal, finance). MEDDPICC's Paper Process component is critical here.\n- Hospital vendor evaluation typically assesses: clinical workflow fit, interoperability, training quality, total cost of ownership, regulatory compliance, implementation timeline.\n- Competitive battlecards are identified as \"crucial\" sales enablement collateral -- should include competitor strengths/weaknesses, objection handling, pricing comparison, and differentiation points.\n- Health IT sales cycles are 6-18 months with 5-15+ stakeholders, making MEDDPICC the optimal qualification framework.\n- **Source**: https://blackbookmarketresearch.com, https://standingpartnership.com/the-anatomy-of-a-battlecard-an-essential-sales-enablement-tool-standing-partnership/\n\n---\n\n## SYNTHESIS: How to Turn Win Probability into Specific Actions\n\nThe research reveals a clear architecture for turning predictive scores into prescriptive actions:\n\n**Layer 1 -- Signal Collection**: CRM data + conversation intelligence + email/calendar activity + intent data + engagement tracking\n\n**Layer 2 -- Predictive Scoring**: ML model trained on 2+ years of won/lost deal patterns assigns a 0-100 deal health score\n\n**Layer 3 -- Gap Analysis**: Compare current deal state against MEDDPICC criteria to identify specific qualification gaps (e.g., \"no Economic Buyer identified,\" \"Decision Process unclear\")\n\n**Layer 4 -- Prescriptive Action Engine**: Based on the gap + deal stage + historical success patterns, recommend specific next actions:\n- \"Schedule executive sponsor meeting (champion alone won't close)\"\n- \"Send ROI calculator -- similar deals closed 40% faster with quantified metrics\"\n- \"Re-engage -- no activity in 12 days, deal at risk of stalling\"\n- \"Loop in legal -- Paper Process undefined with 3 weeks to close date\"\n- \"Send competitive battlecard -- competitor X mentioned in last call\"\n\n**Layer 5 -- Delivery**: Push recommendations to where reps already work (Slack, Teams, CRM, email, mobile notifications) -- not a separate dashboard they won't check.\n\nThe platforms that succeed share one principle: **recommendations must be specific, contextual, and delivered in the flow of work**. Generic alerts (\"deal at risk\") get ignored. Specific actions (\"call the CFO, send the ROI model, reference the Acme case study\") get executed."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5576,"cache_read_input_tokens":93629,"output_tokens":6762,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":5576},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZHZYbuutYVhWAqs3akf2","type":"assistant","uuid":"97aa574b-0db4-4996-9074-13f6e1f5cbe2","timestamp":"2026-03-22T05:27:58.076Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"6fa4d940-41fb-4efd-bc6a-1002703965b6","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"eventual-tinkering-map"}
